< text>
My Boyfriend and I visited this dealership to purchase a used vehicle that we viewed online. It was on the higher end of what we were looking for, but nevertheless its what we wanted. Initially we had found two particular vehicles with the same features and the same mileage but two different colors. This dealership was charging 1000 dollars more than the other vehicle because the car that they had was a more desirable color(black). We negotiated and met in the middle and that was fair for us. It was only costing us 500 dollars more to get a more practical color.

There were a number of things that bothered us but first we were never formally greeted. We called ahead and they knew to be expecting us all the way from Long Beach.. so when we got there they simply said "Ruben?" we said "Yes" and they replied "Come this way". Never  did anyone ask "How are you?", "How was your drive?" or "Thank you for driving out." It didn't really seem as if they appreciated our business. We visited many other dealerships that made us feel more welcomed and even offered us something to drink or snack on. The employees were eating pizza at the desk which usually wouldn't bother me but they were so unfriendly. I felt like we were just another sale to process. I was expecting my experience to be more enjoyable; this was my first time purchasing a car.

They also repeatedly expressed how this particular vehicle had one previous owner and but after running our credit and starting the paper work we found that the car was owned by a rental agency. So technically it had one owner but used by a large amount temporary owners. Nevertheless we agreed it was still the car we wanted but we felt a little deceived. They also advertise that they have a return policy available but while signing papers they required we signed a paper saying we will not return the vehicle.

After all was said and done they handed us ONE key and said they are not obligated to give us two. They explained that its not their job to ask us if we want two and that since we received a deal they would not provide us with another key free of charge. They did end up offering us a discount on the key after complaining but its still going to cost us over 200 dollars for a additional key.

Honestly all the small things that made this experience terrible could have been overseen and me and my boyfriend would have left the lot happy and excited if the customer service was just a little more friendlier. Its all in the way to talk to people. They were just really rude and didn't make us feel like it mattered that we were spending over 30,000 dollars there. Not once did they congratulate us. I was very disappointed with there service and they did not earn my business.<//text>

<user>107133242059644769243<//user><username>Tina Slack<//username>< Text>
On May 1, before arriving at Courtesy Jeep, I was told by the sales person, Ivan, that the vehicle that I wanted to purchase had had the tires swapped out and that if I wanted the over-sized tires that were now on the vehicle, I would need to pay an additional amount over the advertised price.  I advised Ivan that I did not want the over-sized tires, even if they weren't an additional cost.  During the sales process, I was again asked by Ivan and by dealer management and I again told them that I did not want the over-sized tires.  I was told that the tires would be swapped back to the standard size prior to completion of the sale.

After the sale was complete and I was standing at the Jeep, leaving to go home, I was told by Ivan that they had not changed the tires back and that I would need to come back to switch the tires.  I reminded him that I live 1.5 hours from the dealership and that, due to my extremely hectic work and travel schedule, I would not be able to return to the area until the week of June 13.  We agreed that I would come back on June 13.

On May 10, I was pulled over by the CA State Police and discovered that the speedometer was off by 5-8 mph.  I sent an email to Courtesy Jeep asking if I needed to have that repair and the tire changing done by them or if I could use a local Jeep dealership.  My email received no response.

On May 21, I spoke with the Ivan who advised me that I needed to return to the dealership immediately to have the tires changed back.  I reminded him that we had an agreement for me to return on June 13 and I was told that was no longer the case.

I called the service department and made an appointment for May 28.  While talking with the service person, Matthew, I mentioned the problem with the speedometer.  He told me that - of course the speedometer was off - that the wrong size tires were on the vehicle!

I am extremely dissatisfied with my experience with Courtesy Jeep.  I probably would not have made the decision to purchase the Jeep from them if I had know in advance that I would have to return to their location for service after the sale.  I also don't appreciate not being advised that the tires on the vehicle would throw off the speedometer.</Text>

<Date>1399581872852</Date><rating>2< /rating>< Review>
tl;dr:  My story as one of 744,822 customers who have a recall on their occupant restraint control module. A tale of the frustrating and obnoxiously unprofessional customer support that comes with a Chrysler product.

I have the misfortune of owning a Jeep with an occupant restraint control module recall. I found out about the recall in January 2013 using my VIN on the Jeep website. After calling the corporate number, I was told the parts  would be in no later than February 2013 and that I would be notified by mail when they arrived. Every month that I called the ETA would get pushed back and I would receive very little information besides the fact that only a fraction of the 744,822 vehicles affected had caused injuries via inadvertent airbag deployment.

A year later with no notification or letter, I had basically given up and just accepted the fact that my airbags could go off at any moment due to an "electrical overstress." In February 2014, I met an employee of the Irvine Chrysler Dealership and he informed me that they had been doing the M35 ORC repair for months now. This shocked me as the Orange Coast Chrysler dealer had recently told me that they had no parts.

I decided to go into the dealership since I the information I received over the phone was getting me nowhere. They told me they had the new ORC module in stock and could replace it overnight. When I came in for pickup the following morning they informed me that they had to order the part and would notify me when it was ready. So they kept my car for 22 hours to tell me that they still didn‚Äôt have the part.

Over three months later, I finally received an email informing that it‚Äôs time for my next service maintenance. Hopefully this means they have the parts and I can finally be free of this year long headache. I may not be persistent enough but this entire experience has solidified my decision to never purchase a Chrysler product again in this life.<//Review>

<Date>1432152621804</Date><Rating>5< /Rating>< review>
These guys are a little more pricey than the liquor store with the green awning but they are OUTSTANDING!! They can get me beer that Bevmo cannot get me. The last two kegs I bought at Bevmo prior to switching to these guys were off, i.e. flat and oxidized. Should be chance alone, since the whole saler is the same guy for both places. That said, I have not received any bad kegs from Cask and Flask and I am on the fifth one. This is starting to look like a pattern (a very good one). They are incredibly prompt getting the order in and don't have once-a-week processing like Bevmo. Unlike Bevmo, these guys call you when your order is in. They remember who I am and allow me to store the kegs in their cold room until I am ready to pick it up. In summary, these guys are well worth the extra $ you spend on your keg!<//review>

<Rating>4< /Rating><Review>Stopped at Casa de Fruta on the way to Los Banos for much needed rest stop and a bite to eat. Casa de Restaurant had always been a little better than the side of the road cafe.

We did have to wait for a table. It was not that the place was crowded but all of the empty tables needed to be bussed and cleaned. We kept hearing that a table will be ready in a minute for more than 15 minutes.

Since Casa de Fruta is adhering to the Covid19 protocols, out door dining is available. That day was a pleasant 64 degrees so a light jacket was required. They did have a few propane heaters going.

I usually order a chuck of beef but today settled on a club sandwich. The wife had a Casa Burger. The club was good. Nothing really stood out but it was serviceable. The bad is the potato salad. It was way to salty. The Casa burger was better than average. The produce on the burger was fresh. Overall the meal was pleasant.

Our service was a young man and he provided top notch service. Quick on drinks, refills and the requested extra items.

Casa de Fruta is a good place to stop and take a break from driving.<//Review>< Pictures>

<user_id>105529300056545653455<//user_id><Rating>3<//Rating>< Review>
Our trips to the Monterey peninsula usually takes us through Holister and right by this rest stop, which is located on route 152.

The rest stop is a popular stop for tourists and locals alike. With locally grown fruits and vegetables to candies to satisfy even the sweetest of tooth. There is plenty to see and do here for everyone.

There is an elaborate playground to include a carousel and an actual miniature train ride for younger children.

There is a wine tasting room to a candy shop and restaurant on grounds. Anyone ambitious enough can even setup their tent in the nearby campground and there is even room for RV's.

After our usual sightseeing of the surrounding grounds we decided to sit down for lunch at the "Casa De Restaurant."

We stopped in on Easter Sunday and was greeted by waitresses dressed in bunny outfits.

The food at the restaurant isn't known for anything special other than "home cooked meals."

I ordered their fried chicken and in my opinion disappointed. The chicken had no flavor, tough to chew on, and looked like it was prepared yesterday. The mashed potato and gravel was the best part. The side dish of broccoli was wilted along with the carrots.

We ordered cinnamon rolls but it took them over 30 minutes to arrive because they forgot the order. This was also the case with coffee refills.

Although our dining experience was disappointing the overall atmosphere here at this rest stop was very nice and I would recommend anyone to stop in and judge for yourself.< /Review>

My other daughter had the pulled pork and said the meat was super dry and the bread disintegrated the first time she picked it up.  She had to eat it with a fork because the bread had no integrity and was sitting in a pool of juice.  I had the prime rib dip as it was listed as a specialty and was hopeful it would be good.  The meat was terribly over cooked and grey with no flavor.  It tasted as if it had been boiled.  Half of my sandwich was gristle and as my bread did not hold together either.  It was super hot inside the restaurant (it was 106 outside to be fair).  If you can hold out, I would keep going and not stop here to eat.  Its an interesting novelty but the food was awful.<//review>

< review>
Interesting architecture,  definitely feels old school.   Not particularly ornate as the Pantages  theatre in Hollywood,  still has an amazing feel of authenticity.

The Los Angeles Ballet performance of The Nutcracker in December was delightful.  From the balcony, we could see the entire stage come to life.  My kids enjoyed the ballet, especially my 10 year old daughter.

The audio was good, with ample sound for a classical performance. We will visit again for a concert.  Parking was about a mile walk, but we enjoyed walking through the historic UCLA campus.</review>

<response>None< /response>< Review>
I went to see Tigran Hamasyan play here at Royce Hall and I must say that my experience was rather unfortunate.

I want to point out that while I had a great time at the concert, the staffers at Royce Hall did a relatively terrible job managing the show because while a show is going on, it seems that the ushers let people in as the concert in progress. I understand that this is to let people, who paid for their tickets, in but when it gets to the point that so many people are being let in at 20-30 minute intervals and to the point that the performer himself actually has to stop the concert just to let people take their seats, that just completely ruins the experience for everyone. I truly hope that the staff at Royce Hall is made aware of this because if this is a common practice at the performing center, they should know that letting huge groups of people in during the concert just spoils the performance. It is just rude and inconsiderate to the performer and the audience and it would perhaps be ideal to at least let the tardy people come in at the proper timing instead of during a song.< /Review>
